            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

    <tr>
        
        
        <tr id="so3" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Aviles has a chance to make a significant fantasy impact this season if he's not jerked around in Kansas City again. He broke out in 2008 by hitting .325 with 10 home runs in 102 games.  In May of 2009, he went on the DL with a forearm injury and eventually had Tommy John surgery. He came back in 2010 to play 110 games, posting a .304 average and eight home runs. He hit for average during the entire season, but in September and October he hit six of his eight taters. It appears as though Aviles' injury may have been sapping his power for most of the season. One of his traits that can't be overlooked is his position versatility. For the 2011 season he is qualified at second base and shortstop in most leagues. There has been some talk out of the KC camp that he may be holding down third base until top prospect Mike Moustakas is called up, possibly in early June. Aviles' greatest value would likely be as a second baseman.  His 2010 batting average of .304 was fourth-highest among second basemen with 300 PAs or more. One big question make for Aviles is how many games he'll be able to play as well as at what position. He should be drafted in AL leagues and some deep NL leagues. (Jeff Zimmerman)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Mike seems to have finally shaken off his 2009 injury and could be a nice fantasy sleeper.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so4" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>The Red Sox committed to Aviles as their utility infielder in 2012 after trading Jed Lowrie to Houston, and then upped the ante by trading away Marco Scutaro. Aviles might even get into an offense/defense platoon with Nick Punto at short, which would make him a sleeper in deeper leagues. He put together some nice fantasy seasons with the Royals in 2008 (.325, 10 home runs, eight RBI) and 2010 (.304, eight home runs, 14 stolen bases), and even last year he managed to swat seven homers and steal 14 bases in just 91 games (309 plate appearances). Just 19.8% of his career balls in play have been pulled though, so Aviles won't get too much help from the Green Monster during his home games at Fenway, where routine fly balls to left turn into doubles. There's a chance he could see some time in right field against left-handed pitchers, but those starts figure to be few and far between. Aviles has value if he can get his batting average back over .300, but he won't have a ton of power or speed. (Mike Axisa)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Aviles could provide double-digit homers and steals with regular playing time, but it remains to be seen how the Red Sox infield will shake out in 2012. </td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so5" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Aviles was a surprising source of modest power in 2012, but was bounced from Boston to Toronto to Cleveland this offseason. Even if he manages to find quasi-regular at bats behind Asdrubal Cabrera and Jason Kipnis (unlikely, barring injury), he will offer a bit of pop but will probably hurt owners in leagues that reward on-base percentage more than he will help. (<a href="http://www.twitter.com/soxczar">Colin Zarzycki</a>)</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>In a full season, as a full-time player, there is reason to think you could get a 15-15 year out of Mike Aviles. After a 13 homer, 14 bag campaign in Boston in 2012, he put up nine homers and eight stolen bases in just 394 plate appearances in Cleveland. The problem is Aviles still doesn't appear to have an everyday job. There was talk the Tribe could trade Asdrubal Cabrera and let Aviles handle short until prospect Francisco Lindor was ready to take over. But with Jhonny Peralta signing in St. Louis, perhaps Cabrera's most logical destination, it looks like Aviles is going to play a super-utility role again. And for fantasy owners, the lack of playing time is a real concern. If he ends up playing daily or close to it, he's not a terrible option for a middle infield slot, particularly in deeper leagues. (<a href="https://twitter.com/chadyoung">Chad Young</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>When he has played, Aviles has produced. Nothing huge, but enough to be on your radar if he gets an everyday job. There isn't one for him as of today, but if Asdrubal Cabrera gets moved, Aviles gets a big boost.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Mike Aviles is a super-utility man with an 80-grade personality. For those two reasons, and those two reasons alone, the Indians picked up his $3 million option for 2015, despite his replacement-level performance over the last two seasons. Aviles' bat used to be nice for a utility man, but four consecutive seasons of declining power combined with a nonexistent walk rate makes him pretty useless at the plate. At 34, it's tough to see the power coming back, and Aviles will struggle to reach the ~400 plate appearance he's been given the last two years on a deep roster in Cleveland. (<a href="https://twitter.com/AugustF_ABJ">August Fagerstrom</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Aviles will serve the same role he has the last two seasons as a super utility man in Cleveland, but likely in a more limited role. His declining power and terrible on-base skills make him easy to pass over in fantasy.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Aviles carved out a solid role for himself in Cleveland the last couple years, particularly against lefties. Now in Detroit, Aviles seems to have a super-utility role again, but the "super" might only come from the number of positions played as opposed to the production while playing them. Even with playing time, Aviles just doesn't bring much to the table for fantasy owners. He put up a full-season pace of 10 homers and six stolen bases last year, but for a guy without middle-infield eligibility, that isn't useful. His rates are bad for traditional leagues (.265 career average, .231 last year) and even worse for on-base leagues (.297 and .282, respectively). He does offer a favorable platoon split (he hits lefties better), but not a big enough one to be a difference-maker. The Tigers will probably take advantage of that split, but there just isn't a lot for fantasy managers to look at here. (Chad Young)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Mike Aviles doesn't play much, he doesn't have an elite power/speed combo, and his rates are awful. He doesn't offer a strong platoon split to take advantage of, either.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        
    </tr>
